I walked in and I was quite impressed because of course, its a new nail salon so everything is brand new. But Unfortunately that means nothing when it comes to sanitation. Aside from what everyone else is complaining about on the reviews, such as the women in the front not being friendly, but that's not a deal breaker for me. I was told to sit down and was not told how long it was going to take for a good 20 minutes, nobody kept me posted or anything...but still not a deal breaker for me.

What made me walk out was when I saw them not using Disposable Foot Tub Liners. You would think there would be some type of  health regulation at this point in 2018, but regardless as a business owner that is something to consider. It blows my mind, when I see nail salons not having them. You could argue and say they sanitize after its done being used. but as a customer I have to witness that before wanting to put my feet in a tub where hundreds of people do. Unless you're going to sanitize your tubs in front of your customers, you really should invest in some disposable tub liners.</text>

I started going to Woof and Purr Vet earlier this year.  I have a 5 year old Aussie/Collie mix - Dr. Jayme cleaned her teeth and put her on the right flea medication to keep those little buggers from biting.

I recently got a Siberian Husky puppy - when I brought him home he had a terrible case of fleas as well as giardia.  Just like with my Aussie, Dr. Jayme made sure that the fleas were eradicated and the giardia was treated.  I was also skeptical about his first round of shots, so she was more than willing to look at the brand and make her own suggestions as to the next step, choosing to redo his 8-week shots was completely my decision.

She makes a lot of helpful suggestions for different products, but she is never pushy.  They're added to the bill at the end so you can see the price and remember what she recommended, but if you don't want them then its super easy to take them off the bill and just pay for the services/products you want.

Because she runs the vet by herself and only has a few staff members on hand, there have been a few times where I've had to wait for her to finish up or for paperwork to be found, but she's been really accommodating the few instances there has been an issue.  Overall, she is a great vet and I'd highly recommend her.<//text>

< Text>
I took my 2003 Lincoln Navigator in to have the transmission drained, flushed, and the filter replaced, and diagnose the reason for the Check Engine light being on. Original estimate: $275. I left my vehicle to walk home, and before I got home Bill called to say "Bad news, you need a transmission rebuild." I was quoted $2800, but i needed my vehicle, so i said to do the work. That was Friday, June 5th. I called when it was supposed to be done the following Wednesday, but they needed more time. Bill authorized unnecessary parts totalling over $300 and informed me later. On Friday, June 12th, Bill called to say "Your vehicle is done, but I wouldn't drive it!" With the invoice now at $3200, Bill said the Check Engine code was a catalytic converter. If I did not replace it, my engine would blow. Another estimate of $1000 + labor and possibly some miscellaneous parts, but he could get it completed that day. Against my better judgment, I authorized the catalytic converter replacement. When I went to pick up my vehicle, the new total was $4849.63. That's more than I paid for the vehicle 2 years ago!
I maxed out 3 credit cards and took my vehicle. The next morning, my Check Engine light came on again. I took it in and Bill said "No problem, the new catalytic converter needed to sync up with the old one....drive it as much as you want."
He reset the Check Engine light. I told him it still shifted hard, but he claimed it would improve as the lubricant in the new transmission circulated. The light came back on that afternoon. By Monday, my transmission light was flashing as well. When I called Bill on Tuesday morning, he said to bring it in. After work, I was heading to Precision, but didn't make it. The engine blew up 3 blocks from work in San Jose. I had the vehicle towed in.
Bill's offer to make this right is this: He found a used engine (with 100,000 miles) I could buy for $2000, and they would DC discount tug he labor to install it! My transmission is under warranty, but they refuse to fix it until I buy an engine.
So it is July 27th, I am out $4000 and now have a blown engine from the faulty transmission work. My vehicle is still sitting in their lot, and the person they misrepresented as "the owner" of the business is actually the District Manager who didn't call me for 3 weeks, then failed to call back the next day as promised. I finally called Dan back on Wednesday, July 25th, and he is stonewalling me. I asked him to meet me at the facility and we could pull up the error codes, but he told me to take it wherever I wanted for a "2nd opiniom."
DO NOT USE THESE GUYS FOR ANYTHING BUT AN OIL CHANGE. Good luck.<//Text>

He was very helpful and courteous. After the test drive, I decided to buy it. I told Ivan that I was not ready to buy it that night; but, I will be back next day by 2:00 pm with my checks and financing in hand, no financing needed. I could read his face that he did not believe that we were going to be back next day.

We went back the following day at 2:00 pm as planned. We were greeted by Ivan and I told him that we wanted to check the car out for last time. We went outside to look for the vehicle and the vehicle was out doing a test drive. Now, the vehicle was kind of dirty and one of the guy that was doing the test drive was smoking next to the car; I thought that this place was smoking free area. Anyway, I decided to get the car.

We went to his cubicle and he gave me a loan application. Loan application? I told him that I have the checks in hand, no financing needed. He called another coworker, very nice guy and he explained that they don‚Äôt take any check due to frauds. They couldn‚Äôt guarantee if the checks were not fake and find out who I was. So, I told him if you want, we can come tomorrow and call our bank to verify, but refused. According to him they need to run the credit to make sure the check is ok. Credit with check? I can have a very good credit and a bad check or vice versa‚Ä¶ another employee said that the check needs 10 days to clear‚Ä¶inside of myself I was saying full of it‚Ä¶the reality is that acting as a financing middleman is one of the top ways dealers make money. So even if you walk into the dealership with a wad of cash or a pre approved auto loan you got on your own, the dealer has a financial incentive to persuade you to change your mind and apply for a loan affiliated with his dealership which is fine; which is not fine is wasting my time and made me feel that I was using fraud checks! So, we can not buy neither cash nor financing in hand anymore!  I left with a doubt in my mind regarding this matter; would it will be the same treatment if I was not Latino?

< Text>
I want to describe what a 1-day purchase, 5-star review should be from the eyes of the customer, as this is precisely what I received from Stephen Rumph at Rusnak/Pasadena Porsche.

I had been watching Porsche Macans the past few weeks online, and woke up to do my usually searching. I came across one I really liked, and sent the usual message. You know the process from there, and I got connected with Stephen very quickly.

That's when it started to quickly accelerate from from a "typical" online-car-buying experience to a 5-star experience.

I called Stephen as I was concerned living all the way down in San Diego; I didn't want to drive up to Pasadena to potentially take the vehicle home until I knew all about it. Stephen took time to answer my many questions, my repeated call backs, and my repeated emails, and made me feel very safe and comfortable throughout the entire process.

But it went even a step further once we arrive later that evening at the dealership. Stephen took more care than anyone I had ever seen in discussing the details and intricacies of the vehicle. He pointed out numerous things to me that I wasn't even aware of, even after a few weeks of doing my own "homework." By the time we left the dealership with the car, I felt like I knew Stephen as much more than a guy selling me a car, but someone who genuinely cared about our experience and who was just naturally a good person.

This was particularly impactful for my wife and I as this is our first Porsche, and even just walking through the doors of the dealerships like we had been doing the past few weeks can be quite intimidating to rookies like us.

If you're wanting to buy a luxury vehicle--especially Porsche--and want to get connected with someone who will patiently walk you through the entire process and make you feel incredibly comfortable, Stephen Rumph is your guy.

100% impressed. 100% satisfied...now, time to hit the road!<//Text>
